Faith and Disbelief
beginner
4 min
Faith as Heart's Affirmation: Maturidi on Sin and Iman
Maturidi defines iman as tasdiq and explains that sins do not nullify it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's definition of iman as tasdiq al-qalb (heart's affirmation) and why sins do not nullify faith.

Core Idea
Faith is the heart's affirmation; sins do not remove it unless they destroy that affirmation.

This passage from Imam Maturidi clarifies one of the most important topics in Islamic theology: the nature of faith and its relationship to sin. Maturidi presents a precise definition of iman as the heart's inner conviction, and explains that sinful actions, however serious, do not automatically expel a person from faith. You will read his argument and the psychological factors he identifies as leads to sin.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to get a sense of Maturidi's flow.
Notice the tight link between definition and consequence.
2
Identify the definition of iman
Locate the sentence where Maturidi defines iman. What is it? What does leaving faith mean according to him?
The definition is explicit: 'al-iman huwa tasdiq al-qalb'.
3
Understand the relation between sins and faith
Find the statement that sins do not affect faith. Under what condition? Note the phrase 'ma damat la tu'aththir al-tasdiq fi al-qulub'.
4
Reflect on the universality of minor sins
Maturidi states that everyone commits minor sins. Why? How does this relate to human nature?
He mentions the ability to do good and evil.
5
Examine the psychological factors
List the factors Maturidi gives that lead to sin. They are: shahwa, ghafla, ghadab, hamiyya, and raja' al-'afw. Understand each.
These factors show that sin does not necessarily imply disbelief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد نستطيع أن نفهم الماتريدي من خلال نظرته إلى الدين بأن الإسلام دين يسهل اعتناقه ويصعب تركه . فالإيمان عبارة عنده عن تصديق القلب الحقائق الدين؛ والخروج عن الإيمان یعنی ترك تلك الحقائق الدينية. وأما الذنوب التي هي عبارة عن معاملات سيئة فلن يتأثر بها الإيمان ما دامت لا تؤثر التصديق في القلوب. ومن المعلوم أنه ليس هناك أحد لا يرتكب الصغيرة، لأن الإنسان خُلق وهو عنده القدرة على فعلي الخير والشر. وفي القرآن الكريم أمثلة حول الأنبياء الذين صدرت منهم زلات فبكوا من أجلها بالحضرة الإلهية وهم يعرضون حالتهم هذه، فدعوا الله تضرعًا وخوفاً . وقد ذكر الماتريدي العوامل النفسية التي تؤدي بالمرء إلى ارتكاب المعاصي، فيشير إلى أنه دفعته إليها الغلبة من شهوة أو غفلة أو شدة الغضب والحمية، أو رجاء العفو والتوبة من غير استحلال منه ولا استخفاف.
And we can understand Maturidi through his view of religion: that Islam is a religion easy to embrace and difficult to leave. For faith (al-iman) according to him is the heart's affirmation (tasdiq) of religious truths; and leaving faith means abandoning those religious truths. As for sins (al-dhunub), which are bad actions, they do not affect faith as long as they do not affect the affirmation in hearts. And it is known that there is no one who does not commit minor sins, because man was created with the ability to do both good and evil. In the Noble Qur'an there are examples of prophets who made slips and wept for them in the divine presence, presenting their state, so they called upon God in supplication and fear. And Maturidi mentioned the psychological factors that lead a person to commit sins, indicating that he is driven to them by predominance of desire, heedlessness, intense anger and zeal, or hope of pardon and repentance without regarding them as permissible or belittling them.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage explains Maturidi's concept of faith (iman) and its relation to sin. Maturidi defines iman as 'tasdiq al-qalb' (the heart's affirmation) of religious truths. Thus, leaving faith is abandoning those truths. Sins, which are bad actions (mu'amalat sayyi'a), do not affect faith unless they impact the heart's affirmation. Maturidi then notes that everyone commits minor sins, as humans have the capacity for good and evil. He cites examples from the Qur'an where prophets made slips and repented sincerely. Then he lists psychological factors that lead to sin: predominance of desire (shahwa), heedlessness (ghafla), intense anger (ghadab) and zeal (hamiyya), or hope of pardon and repentance without considering the sin as permissible or belittling it. This shows Maturidi's nuanced view that sinfulness does not automatically negate faith.

Key Terms
الإيمان
تصديق القلب
الذنوب
الصغيرة
العوامل النفسية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that committing any sin automatically removes a person from faith.
Correction: Maturidi clarifies that faith remains as long as the heart's affirmation is intact; sins do not nullify faith unless they destroy that affirmation.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is iman (faith)?
A) Verbal profession only
B) Actions of the limbs
C) The heart's affirmation (tasdiq) of religious truths
D) Both belief and actions

Key Takeaway
For Maturidi, iman is the heart's affirmation of religious truths, and sins do not negate it as long as that affirmation remains intact.

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
4 min
Maturidi on the Positions of Khawarij and Mu'tazila
Maturidi presents the views of Khawarij and Mu'tazila and criticizes them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the positions of the Khawarij and Mu'tazila on major sins and Maturidi's severe critique that they oppose text, reason, and reality.

Core Idea
Maturidi rejects the extremes of Khawarij and Mu'tazila on major sins.

The Khawarij and Mu'tazila held that major sins expel one from faith, but Maturidi sharply criticizes these views as contradicting revelation, reason, and reality. This lesson presents their opinions and Maturidi's response.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the views
Read the Arabic passage once to understand the opinions of the Khawarij and Mu'tazila regarding major sins. Then read the translation.
Notice the three positions: kufr, expulsion from iman, and hypocrisy.
2
Identify Maturidi's criticisms
Maturidi describes the adherents as opponents of text, reason, and reality, and as unjust. Think about why he uses such strong language.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider how Maturidi's critique sets the stage for his own positive analysis in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لقد أفاد الماتريدي بأن البعض من الخوارج يعتقدون أن الذنوب كلها، صغيرها وكبيرها، تخرج المؤمن عن دائرة الدين كما أشار إلى أن أغلب الخوارج ومتكلمي المعتزلة يعتقدون بأن ارتكاب الكبيرة يخرج صاحبه عن الإيمان فمرتكب الكبيرة عند الخوارج يكفر، وعند المعتزلة لا يكفر رغم خروجه عن الإيمان. والبعض يرى أنه منافق. فالماتريدي يشير إلى جميع تلك الآراء ويذكر أدلتهم، ثم يوجه إليهم انتقادات شديدة اللهجة، فيصف منتحليهم بأنهم معارضون للنص والعقل والواقع وأنهم غير منصفين. فالماتريدي الذي يحلل الحالة النفسية للمؤمن الذي يعرض أحوالاً قبيحة أو الإهمال السيئ، فهو من ناحية أولى يشير إلى مطابقته للواقع في المجتمع الإسلامي، ومن ناحية أخرى يقدم أمثلة للأخلاق النبوي الموصوف بأنه رؤف رحيم للمؤمنين. ويعني ذلك في نظره أنه ما من أحد يعصى الله بنوع من الكبائر دون الشرك إلا وهو في حالة ارتكاب الكبيرة مكتسب الطاعة نفسيا؛ فإنه يحمل في داخل نفسه أحاسيس الخوف من العقاب الإلهي، والفزع عن مقته تعالى، والرجاء برحمته والثقة بكرمه. فهذه الأحاسيس التي تظهر في صورة خيرات في نفسه فهي الأحاسيس التي قد تكون غالبة على الذنوب التي ارتكبها بغلبة الأسباب الدافعة إلى تلك السيئات. فعلينا في هذا النطاق أن نتذكر ببعض ما أنعم الله على رتكب الكبيرة من النعم؛ فقد أحسن الله إليه بوضع حب الله تعالى وحب أوليائه في قلبه، كما أعطى له الإحساس باحترام الحق الإلهي وحقوق أوليائه. فالله تعالى يؤمّن خلقه بأن لا يضيع جميع ما أكرمهم به من هذه النعم. وفى الحقيقة فإن الناس جميعًا، وإن اختلفت أديانهم التي اعتقدوها، يصممون أن يقفوا صادقين أمام معتقداتهم، وينفرون عن معاملات تبعدهم من أديانهم، فلن تتغير النتائج وإن كانوا اعتقدوها عن طريق الاستدلال العقلى أو المعجزة أو التقليد. وقد ذكرنا الماتريدي مشيرًا إلى آية قرآنية بأن الابتعاد عن الكبائر يسبب العفو عن الصغائر. ومما لا شك فيه أن التوبة أيضًا وسيلة لمغفرة جميع أنواع الذنوب. وأما الكبائر من الذنوب ـ فيما عدا الشرك والكفر - فيمكن العفو عنها بكون المذنب قد عفاه الله الرحمن.
Maturidi informed that some of the Khawarij believe that all sins, minor and major, expel the believer from the circle of religion, and he indicated that most of the Khawarij and the theologians of the Mu'tazila believe that committing a major sin (kabira) expels its doer from iman. So according to the Khawarij, the committer of a major sin becomes a disbeliever (kafir), and according to the Mu'tazila, he does not become a disbeliever despite being expelled from iman. And some see that he is a hypocrite (munafiq). Maturidi refers to all these opinions and mentions their evidences, then directs severe criticisms to them, describing their adherents as opponents of text, reason, and reality, and as unjust. Maturidi, who analyzes the psychological state of the believer who commits ugly acts or serious neglect, on one hand points to its correspondence with reality in Islamic society, and on the other hand gives examples of prophetic character described as 'kind and merciful to the believers'. This means in his view that there is no one who disobeys Allah by any type of major sin other than shirk except that he, while committing the major sin, psychologically acquires obedience; for he carries inside himself feelings of fear of divine punishment, dread of His wrath, hope for His mercy, and trust in His generosity. These feelings, which appear as good qualities in his soul, are the feelings that may overcome the sins he committed due to the predominance of the causes driving to those evil deeds. Therefore in this context we must remember some of the blessings that Allah has bestowed upon the committer of major sins: Allah has favored him by placing love of Allah and love of His saints in his heart, and gave him a sense of respect for divine right and the rights of His saints. So Allah Almighty ensures His creation that He will not waste all these blessings with which He honored them. In fact, all people, even if their religions differ, are determined to stand sincerely before their beliefs, and they shrink from actions that distance them from their religions. The results will not change even if they believed through rational inference, miracle, or imitation. And Maturidi mentioned, referring to a Quranic verse, that avoiding major sins causes forgiveness for minor sins. There is no doubt that repentance (al-tawba) is also a means of forgiveness for all kinds of sins. As for the major sins – other than shirk and kufr – forgiveness is possible if the sinner is pardoned by Allah, the Most Merciful.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage presents Maturidi's refutation of the extreme positions of the Khawarij and the Mu'tazila regarding major sins (kabira). Maturidi reports the views: the Khawarij say major sins make one a disbeliever; the Mu'tazila say they expel from iman but not to kufr; some say he is a hypocrite. Maturidi criticizes these views severely, calling their proponents opposed to text, reason, and reality. Then he provides his own psychological analysis: a believer who commits a major sin (except shirk) still has inner feelings of fear of punishment, dread of Allah's wrath, hope for mercy, and trust in generosity. These feelings constitute a form of inner obedience. Therefore, the sinner retains some good qualities, such as love of Allah and His saints, and respect for divine rights. Allah does not waste these blessings. Maturidi also cites a Quranic principle that avoiding major sins results in forgiveness for minor sins. Finally, he emphasizes that repentance (tawba) can forgive all sins, and major sins (other than shirk and kufr) can be forgiven by Allah's mercy. This shows Maturidi's middle path: he affirms that major sins do not nullify iman, nor do they make the sinner a kafir, while also holding that forgiveness is possible through repentance and divine mercy.

Key Terms
الخوارج
المعتزلة
الكبيرة
الإيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that Maturidi completely absolves the sinner, but here he merely critiques the extreme positions.
Correction: Maturidi's criticism is directed at the Khawarij and Mu'tazila, not at the severity of sin itself.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the common flaw of the Khawarij and Mu'tazila views on major sins?
A) They are too lenient on sin
B) They contradict text, reason, and reality
C) They deny the concept of faith
D) They agree with each other

Key Takeaway
Maturidi considers the Khawarij and Mu'tazila views on major sins as extreme and contradictory to revelation, reason, and reality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see a Muslim committing a major sin, are you quick to label them as 'bad' or 'hypocrite'? How does Maturidi's harsh critique of those who judge extremes challenge your own tendency to judge others harshly? Will you commit to seeing sinners as fellow believers in need of guidance rather than labels?
?
Have you ever minimized your own sin by thinking, 'It's not that bad, I still have iman'? How does Maturidi's rejection of both the Khawarij and Mu'tazila positions expose the danger of rationalizing sin? Will you stop using theological labels to excuse your own disobedience?
?
If Maturidi calls the proponents of these views 'opponents of text, reason, and reality,' what does that say about your own reasoning when you adopt extreme positions on sin? Are you willing to let the Qur'an and sound reason correct your attitudes toward sinners, even if it means being more merciful?

Maturidi's Psychological Analysis of the Sinner
Maturidi analyzes the inner state of a major sinner and affirms the possibility of forgiveness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that a believer who commits a major sin still retains inner feelings of faith and obedience, and that repentance and divine mercy can forgive such sins.

Core Idea
The sinner's inner fear and hope are signs of continued faith.

Maturidi goes beyond critique to offer a positive analysis: even when committing a major sin, the believer's psychological state reflects a continuing connection to Allah. This lesson explores that inner dimension and its consequences for forgiveness.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the psychological state
Read the Arabic passage about the believer who commits a major sin. Notice the feelings described: fear, dread, hope, trust.
2
Identify the signs of retained faith
Maturidi mentions love of Allah and His saints, and respect for divine rights. List these as signs that faith remains.
3
Understand the role of repentance and mercy
Maturidi concludes that avoiding major sins brings forgiveness for minor ones, and repentance can forgive all sins, including major ones through Allah's mercy.
This distinguishes Maturidi's view from the Khawarij and Mu'tazila.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لقد أفاد الماتريدي بأن البعض من الخوارج يعتقدون أن الذنوب كلها، صغيرها وكبيرها، تخرج المؤمن عن دائرة الدين كما أشار إلى أن أغلب الخوارج ومتكلمي المعتزلة يعتقدون بأن ارتكاب الكبيرة يخرج صاحبه عن الإيمان فمرتكب الكبيرة عند الخوارج يكفر، وعند المعتزلة لا يكفر رغم خروجه عن الإيمان. والبعض يرى أنه منافق. فالماتريدي يشير إلى جميع تلك الآراء ويذكر أدلتهم، ثم يوجه إليهم انتقادات شديدة اللهجة، فيصف منتحليهم بأنهم معارضون للنص والعقل والواقع وأنهم غير منصفين. فالماتريدي الذي يحلل الحالة النفسية للمؤمن الذي يعرض أحوالاً قبيحة أو الإهمال السيئ، فهو من ناحية أولى يشير إلى مطابقته للواقع في المجتمع الإسلامي، ومن ناحية أخرى يقدم أمثلة للأخلاق النبوي الموصوف بأنه رؤف رحيم للمؤمنين. ويعني ذلك في نظره أنه ما من أحد يعصى الله بنوع من الكبائر دون الشرك إلا وهو في حالة ارتكاب الكبيرة مكتسب الطاعة نفسيا؛ فإنه يحمل في داخل نفسه أحاسيس الخوف من العقاب الإلهي، والفزع عن مقته تعالى، والرجاء برحمته والثقة بكرمه. فهذه الأحاسيس التي تظهر في صورة خيرات في نفسه فهي الأحاسيس التي قد تكون غالبة على الذنوب التي ارتكبها بغلبة الأسباب الدافعة إلى تلك السيئات. فعلينا في هذا النطاق أن نتذكر ببعض ما أنعم الله على رتكب الكبيرة من النعم؛ فقد أحسن الله إليه بوضع حب الله تعالى وحب أوليائه في قلبه، كما أعطى له الإحساس باحترام الحق الإلهي وحقوق أوليائه. فالله تعالى يؤمّن خلقه بأن لا يضيع جميع ما أكرمهم به من هذه النعم. وفى الحقيقة فإن الناس جميعًا، وإن اختلفت أديانهم التي اعتقدوها، يصممون أن يقفوا صادقين أمام معتقداتهم، وينفرون عن معاملات تبعدهم من أديانهم، فلن تتغير النتائج وإن كانوا اعتقدوها عن طريق الاستدلال العقلى أو المعجزة أو التقليد. وقد ذكرنا الماتريدي مشيرًا إلى آية قرآنية بأن الابتعاد عن الكبائر يسبب العفو عن الصغائر. ومما لا شك فيه أن التوبة أيضًا وسيلة لمغفرة جميع أنواع الذنوب. وأما الكبائر من الذنوب ـ فيما عدا الشرك والكفر - فيمكن العفو عنها بكون المذنب قد عفاه الله الرحمن.

Commentary

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that Maturidi teaches that major sins are automatically forgiven without repentance.
Correction: Maturidi emphasizes that avoiding major sins and repentance are means, but ultimately forgiveness is by Allah's mercy.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what feelings does a believer who commits a major sin (other than shirk) still possess?
A) Only fear of punishment
B) Fear, hope, trust, and love
C) Despair and hopelessness
D) Hypocrisy and doubt

Key Takeaway
Maturidi argues that the inner state of a major sinner includes feelings of faith and obedience, and through repentance and divine mercy, major sins can be forgiven.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you recognize in yourself the feelings of fear of Allah's punishment and hope for His mercy? Or have you become numb to them? What might that numbness reveal about the state of your faith?
?
Maturidi says that even the sinner carries love for Allah and His saints in his heart. Think of a time you sinned: did you still feel that love? If yes, how did you respond? If not, what does that tell you about the condition of your heart?
?
This passage offers immense hope, but also reminds that repentance is essential. Are you using this hope as an excuse to continue sinning, or does it drive you to turn back to Allah in sincere repentance? Which direction will you choose today?

Faith and Disbelief
beginner
4 min
Means of Forgiveness for Major Sins
Maturidi enumerates means of forgiveness for major sins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the multiple means through which Allah may forgive major sins according to Maturidi.

Core Idea
Forgiveness of major sins is possible through many paths, not just repentance.

In this passage, Imam al-Maturidi outlines the various ways Allah can forgive major sins (excluding shirk and kufr). He begins by citing a Qur'anic principle that avoiding major sins leads to forgiveness of minor ones, then lists several other means including repentance, punishment, good deeds, and intercession.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of means
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, noting each means Maturidi mentions.
The list includes abstaining from major sins, repentance, direct forgiveness, punishment, good deeds, and intercession.
2
Note the exception of shirk and kufr
Maturidi excludes polytheism and disbelief from the scope of these means.
This aligns with the Islamic consensus that shirk and kufr are unforgivable unless repented before death.
3
Understand repentance as a general means
Repentance is mentioned as a means for all types of sins, including major ones.
Repentance is a powerful tool that can erase any sin.
4
Reflect on the inclusivity of divine mercy
The variety of means shows Allah's mercy and wisdom in providing multiple paths to forgiveness.
This counters the notion that major sins are automatically unforgivable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد ذكرنا الماتريدي مشيرًا إلى آية قرآنية بأن الابتعاد عن الكبائر يسبب العفو عن الصغائر . . ومما لا شك فيه أن التوبة أيضًا وسيلة لمغفرة جميع أنواع الذنوب. وأما الكبائر من الذنوب ـ فيما عدا الشرك والكفر - فيمكن العفو عنها بكون المذنب قد عفاه الله الرحمن الرحيم، أو عاقبه في الدنيا أو الآخرة، أو بتقديم العبودية الخالصة أو الأعمال الحسنة ، أو بالنيل إلى شفاعة شفيع . وقد قدم الماتريدي انتقاداته للخوارج والمعتزلة الذين ينكرون في معتقداتهم إمكان العفو عن الذنوب بالشفاعة، ثم يثب لهم بطرق نقلية وعقلية أن الشفاعة حق.
And we have mentioned al-Maturidi, referring to a Qur'anic verse, that abstaining from major sins causes forgiveness of minor sins. And there is no doubt that repentance is also a means for forgiveness of all types of sins. As for major sins — aside from polytheism and disbelief — forgiveness of them is possible by the sinner being forgiven by Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful, or by His punishing him in this world or the Hereafter, or by offering pure worship or good deeds, or by attaining the intercession of an intercessor. And al-Maturidi presented his criticisms to the Khawarij and the Mu'tazila who deny in their beliefs the possibility of forgiveness of sins through intercession, then he established for them through transmitted and rational proofs that intercession is true.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage explains Maturidi's view on forgiveness of sins. It begins by noting that Maturidi cites a verse indicating that avoiding major sins leads to forgiveness of minor sins. Repentance is also a means for all sins. Regarding major sins other than polytheism and disbelief, forgiveness can occur through various means: direct forgiveness from God, punishment in this world or the hereafter, sincere worship and good deeds, or the intercession of an intercessor. Maturidi then criticizes the Khawarij and Mu'tazila who deny the possibility of forgiveness through intercession. He counters them with both transmitted (naqli) and rational (aqli) proofs to affirm that intercession is a reality. The passage thus defends the Sunni doctrine of intercession against those who reject it.

Key Terms
الكبائر
الشرك
الكفر
التوبة
الشفاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT mentioned as a means of forgiveness for major sins?
A) Repentance
B) Faith alone without works
C) Punishment in this world or the Hereafter
D) Intercession

Key Takeaway
Allah's mercy provides many ways for major sins to be forgiven, though shirk and kufr are excluded from intercession.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a major sin you struggle with. Which of the means of forgiveness listed in this lesson do you most rely on? Are you actively using that means, or are you passive? What will you change today?
?
If you were to die tonight with an unrepented major sin, honestly assess: Would you trust that Allah will forgive you through one of the other means? Or does your heart tremble? What does that reveal about your relationship with His mercy?
?
The passage says avoiding major sins causes forgiveness of minor sins. Examine your life: Are you truly avoiding major sins, or do you make excuses? What step will you take this week to guard yourself from one specific major sin?

The Reality of Intercession and Refutation of Deniers
Maturidi refutes sects that deny intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi defends intercession as a means of forgiveness against the denials of the Khawarij and Mu'tazila.

Core Idea
Intercession is a proven reality, supported by scripture and reason.

Maturidi now turns to defend the doctrine of intercession against those who deny it. He criticizes the Khawarij and Mu'tazila for rejecting that intercession can forgive major sins, and then affirms it using both transmitted and rational arguments.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the opposing views
Identify the Khawarij and Mu'tazila as the sects denying intercession.
They believed that major sins without repentance lead to eternal punishment, rejecting intercession.
2
Understand Maturidi's method of refutation
Maturidi uses both transmitted (naqli) and rational (aqli) proofs.
Transmitted proofs come from Quran and Hadith; rational proofs use logical arguments.
3
Note the outcome
Maturidi establishes that intercession is true (haqq).
This aligns with Sunni doctrine that the Prophet and others can intercede on behalf of sinners.

Source Text

According to Maturidi, how does he prove the reality of intercession?

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The Khawarij and Mu'tazila denied intercession because they thought it contradicted God's justice. Do you, in your heart, harbor a similar suspicion? Examine your own assumptions: do you truly believe that God's mercy can override the weight of your sins through intercession, or do you subconsciously think you must earn forgiveness solely through deeds?

Faith and Disbelief
beginner

Maturidi's Definition of Faith as Inner Affirmation
Maturidi states his definition of faith and contrasts it with other sects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that for Imam al-Maturidi, faith is exclusively inner affirmation (tasdiq bil-qalb), and how this differs from sects that include verbal confession and actions.

Core Idea
Faith is only what the heart affirms — not words or deeds.

This passage presents the core of Imam al-Maturidi's definition of faith. While many early Islamic sects argued that faith includes verbal confession and physical actions, al-Maturidi held that faith is solely the inner conviction of the heart. Let's read his position and the arguments he uses.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation to understand the positions described.
Notice that the passage lists several sects that add actions to faith.
2
Identify the opposing view
Find the sentence where the Mu'tazila, Khawarij, etc., define faith as including confession and action. Note the consequence for those who omit them.
3
Identify Maturidi's definition
Locate the sentence stating Maturidi's view: faith is only tasdiq bil-qalb. Observe that he supports it with revealed and rational proof.
4
Reflect on the implications
Think about why this definition matters: if faith is only inner, then outward sin does not remove faith, though it may reduce its perfection.
This distinguishes Maturidis from Khawarij and Mu'tazila.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإيمان والإسلام
ومن المعلوم أن الإيمان الذي يعتبر نقطة انطلاق للحياة الدينية، ودور الإرادة البشرية فيها، والحفاظ على الإيمان والدفاع عنه، يعتبر كل ذلك من الموضوعات التي نوقشت حولها بين المذاهب الإسلامية المختلفة . هذا، فقد خصص الماتريدي القسم الأخير من كتاب التوحيد لتلك المسائل حتى ينسق آرائه الكلامية على أسلوب منهجي. والموضوعات نفسها نراها مختصرة ذكرها الأشعري في اللمع (ص (٧٦٧٥ ، وابن فورك تعرض إليها بتفصيل أكثر في مجرد المقالات ( ص ١٤٩ - ١٦٣) ؛ وكذلك نرى أن المؤلفات المتأخرة من الكلام السني قد تناولت تلك المسائل أيضًا.
إن المعتزلة والخوارج والكرامية والحشوية لعل الماتريدي يقصد بالفرقة الأخيرة بعض السلفيين) يعتقدون أن العمل جزء من الإيمان، فبالتالي يقولون في تعريف الإيمان الذي هو التصديق بالقلب وهم يضيفون إليه الإقرار باللسان والعمل بالجوارح . وبناء على ذلك، فالمرء الذي لا يقر بلسانه ليس بمؤمن في حياة الدنيا، والذي يرتكب الكبيرة يخرج عن الإيمان. فقد ذهب الماتريدي إلى أن الإيمان عبارة عن التصديق بالقلب، ويستدل على ذلك بعديد من الآيات والأحاديث ، ثم يضيف إليها استدلالاته العقلية . إن المناقشة التي جرت حول الإيمان وكونه مخلوقا أو أزليا تعتمد بالتالي على أن الهداية هل هي فعل العبد أم لا. فالماتريدي، وهو ينقل مقولة فرقة من فرق الحشوية» بأنه لو كانت الهداية كلها فعل الله ، فبالتالي سوف يتميز الإيمان باللائحة الإلهية الأزلية، ويعني ذلك أننا لا نستطيع أن ندعى بأن هؤلاء الذين لا يؤمنون بأنهم مكلفون بالإيمان" . إن المعتزلة والخوارج والحشوية لم يسمحوا بأن يقول المرء بأنه مؤمن باليقين، رغم أنهم قد قالوا بأن العمل عنصر
Faith and Islam. And it is known that faith, which is considered the starting point of religious life, and the role of the human will in it, and preserving and defending faith — all of these are subjects that were discussed among the different Islamic sects. This, al-Maturidi devoted the last section of the Book of Tawhid to these issues in order to organize his theological views in a systematic manner. And we see the same subjects briefly mentioned by al-Ash'ari in al-Luma' (p. 75?), and Ibn Furak discussed them in more detail in Mujarrad al-Maqalat (pp. 149-163); and we also see that later works of Sunni theology treated these issues as well. Indeed, the Mu'tazila, Khawarij, Karramiyya, and Hashwiyya — perhaps al-Maturidi means by the last group some Salafis — believe that action is part of faith, so they say in defining faith, which is [inner] affirmation (tasdiq) by the heart, they add to it verbal confession (iqrar bil-lisan) and action (amal bil-jawarih). Consequently, a person who does not confess verbally is not a believer in this worldly life, and one who commits a major sin leaves faith. Al-Maturidi held that faith is [only] affirmation (tasdiq) by the heart, and he argues for this with many verses and hadiths, and then adds his rational arguments. The discussion that took place about faith and whether it is created or eternal depends accordingly on whether guidance is an action of the servant or not. Al-Maturidi, while transmitting the statement of a group of the Hashwiyya, that if all guidance were the act of God, then faith would be distinguished by the eternal divine decree, and that means we cannot claim that those who do not believe are charged with faith. The Mu'tazila, Khawarij, and Hashwiyya did not permit a person to say that he is a believer with certainty, even though they claimed that action is a component
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is a section titled 'Faith and Islam' that presents the debate on the definition of faith. It begins by noting that faith is a central issue discussed among Islamic sects. Maturidi devoted the last part of his book to these matters, and other Sunni theologians like al-Ash'ari and Ibn Furak also addressed them. The passage then states that the Mu'tazila, Khawarij, Karramiyya, and Hashwiyya believe that action is part of faith, so they define faith as inner affirmation (tasdiq bil-qalb) plus verbal confession (iqrar bil-lisan) and action (amal bil-jawarih). Consequently, for them, a person who does not confess verbally is not a believer in this world, and one who commits a major sin leaves faith. In contrast, Maturidi held that faith is exclusively inner affirmation (tasdiq bil-qalb), and he supports this with scriptural and rational arguments. The passage then mentions the related issue of whether guidance (huda) is an act of the servant or of God, and that Maturidi reports a statement from the Hashwiyya that if all guidance is from God, then faith is determined by eternal decree, implying that those who do not believe are not obligated to believe. Finally, the passage notes that the Mu'tazila, Khawarij, and Hashwiyya did not allow a person to say with certainty that he is a believer, even though they considered action as a component (the text is cut off).

Key Terms
الإيمان
التصديق بالقلب
الإقرار باللسان
العمل بالجوارح
الخوارج
المعتزلة
الحشوية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that faith includes actions such as prayer and charity as essential components.
Correction: According to Maturidi, faith is only the inner conviction of the heart; actions are required but not part of the essence of faith.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the definition of faith according to al-Maturidi?
A) Tasdiq bil-qalb only
B) Tasdiq bil-qalb and iqrar bil-lisan
C) Tasdiq bil-qalb, iqrar bil-lisan, and amal bil-jawarih
D) Only amal bil-jawarih

Key Takeaway
For Imam al-Maturidi, faith is solely the inner conviction of the heart, not dependent on outward expressions or deeds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If faith is truly only what your heart affirms, then what does your heart actually affirm right now—not what you say or do, but what you truly believe about Allah and His Messenger? Are there areas where your outward actions exceed your inner conviction? How will you align your heart today?
?
The lesson shows that Maturidi relied on both revelation and reason to define faith. Have you ever critically examined the basis of your own faith? What single proof for the truth of Islam resonates most deeply with your heart, and are you willing to study it further to strengthen your inner tasdiq?

Faith and Disbelief

Guidance, Free Will, and the Limits of Human Obligation
Maturidi reports and critiques the Hashwiyya view on guidance and human obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the connection between guidance (huda) and faith, and why al-Maturidi rejects the idea that all guidance comes from God alone in a way that negates human responsibility.

Core Idea
If all guidance were from God, no one could be blamed for disbelief.

This passage explores a deeper implication of the faith debate: is guidance an act of God or of the servant? Al-Maturidi reports a view from the Hashwiyya that if all guidance is from God, then faith is predetermined and humans are not responsible. We'll examine this argument and its consequences.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice that it links the faith debate to the issue of guidance (huda).
2
Identify the Hashwiyya's argument
Find the statement attributed to the Hashwiyya: if all guidance is God's act, then faith is distinguished by eternal decree, and humans cannot be held accountable.
This is a theological determinism argument.
3
See Maturidi's rejection
Although the passage does not explicitly state Maturidi's own position, it implies he rejects this view by noting the consequence (that those who do not believe would not be obligated).
Maturidi affirms human responsibility.
4
Reflect on the broader significance
Think about how this connects to the earlier definition: if faith is only inner, and if guidance is partly from human will, then humans are accountable.
This is a key Maturidi doctrine on free will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if God guides, humans have no free will or responsibility for faith.
Correction: Maturidi rejects absolute determinism; humans are responsible for accepting guidance, and faith is not merely a divine decree without human choice.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what consequence do the Hashwiyya derive from the premise that all guidance is God's act?
A) Faith is a human creation.
B) Faith is determined by eternal decree and humans are not obligated.
C) Faith includes actions.
D) One must say they are a believer with certainty.

Key Takeaway
Al-Maturidi rejects the determinist conclusion that total divine guidance removes human responsibility; he upholds human free will and obligation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Если бы вы тайно верили, что ваше неверие предопределено Богом, чувствовали бы вы себя ответственным за то, чтобы уверовать? Как этот отрывок разрушает такое оправдание?
?
Есть ли в вашей жизни области, где вы обвиняете обстоятельства или волю Бога в отсутствии веры? Что этот урок говорит вам об этом?
?
Матуриди передаёт, что некоторые секты не позволяли человеку сказать 'я верующий' с уверенностью. А вы уверены в своей вере? Почему да или почему нет? Каков был бы ответ Матуриди?

Maturidi's Rejection of the Exception Phrase in Faith
Maturidi rejects the exception phrase and presents his reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Maturidi rejects the phrase 'I am a believer if Allah wills' and how this reflects his view that faith is certain and action is not part of it.

Core Idea
Faith is certain; no conditional language can be used when affirming it.

In this passage, al-Maturidi addresses a common practice among some Muslims who would say 'I am a believer if Allah wills.' He sees this as a serious error, both in method and in substance. Let's read his argument and understand why he insists that faith must be affirmed without exception.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Maturidi uses a very concise and definitive tone.
2
Identify the two reasons Maturidi gives
The passage presents two key reasons: first, action is not a part of faith; second, using 'if Allah wills' implies hesitation and doubt. Find these in the text.
3
Understand the basis of his rejection
Maturidi concludes that this practice is invalid both by transmitted evidence (samʿan) and reason (ʿaqlan). See how he links the two reasons to this conclusion.
This shows that for Maturidi, faith must be certain and free from doubt.
4
Reflect on the broader implications
Consider how this argument shapes the Maturidi definition of faith as not including actions, and how it distinguishes his school from others.
This is a key point of divergence from other theological schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من عناصر الإيمان، فاقترحوا مثلاً بالاستثناء فيه قائلاً «أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله». فهذا المفهوم لم يلق القبول من قبل الماتريدي وذهب إلى أن هذا الرأي خاطئ أصولاً ومنهجا؛ فالعمل قبل كل شيء ليس بجزء من الإيمان، واستخدام عبارة «إن شاء الله في ساحتي الدين والعقيدة يفيد الحيرة والتردد، وذلك كله غير صحيح سمعا وعقلاً.
From the elements of faith, they proposed, for example, an exception in it by saying: 'I am a believer if Allah wills.' So this concept was not accepted by al-Maturidi, and he held that this opinion is erroneous in fundamentals and methodology; for action, before everything, is not a part of faith, and the use of the phrase 'if Allah wills' in the domains of religion and creed indicates confusion and hesitation, and all of that is incorrect by transmitted evidence (samʿan) and reason (ʿaqlan).
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage presents al-Maturidi's position on a specific theological issue: whether one may say 'I am a believer if Allah wills.' It begins by noting that some people proposed making an exception in affirming faith by adding the condition 'if Allah wills.' Al-Maturidi rejects this concept entirely. He argues that this opinion is fundamentally and methodologically wrong. The reasoning is twofold: first, action is not a part of faith (so uncertainty about actions does not affect the certainty of faith itself), and second, using the phrase 'if Allah wills' in the domain of religion and creed creates a sense of doubt and hesitation. Al-Maturidi concludes that this practice is invalid both on the basis of transmitted scripture (samʿan) and reason (ʿaqlan). The passage thus defines a key Maturidī tenet: faith is not composed of acts, and it must be affirmed with certainty, without conditional language that implies doubt.

Key Terms
الإيمان (al-īmān)
الاستثناء (al-istithnā')
العمل (al-ʿamal)
السمع (al-samʿ)
العقل (al-ʿaql)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the disagreement is merely about politeness or humility, but Maturidi's objection is doctrinal: it concerns the nature of faith itself.
Correction: Maturidi's rejection is not about etiquette; it is about the certainty of faith. Using 'if Allah wills' implies doubt about one's faith, which contradicts the nature of faith as certain and unwavering.

Checkpoint
Why does al-Maturidi reject saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills'?
A) Because it implies doubt about one's faith.
B) Because it is forbidden to use the phrase 'if Allah wills' in any context.
C) Because action is a part of faith and one must be uncertain about actions.
D) Because it is not mentioned in the Quran or Sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Al-Maturidi rejects the phrase 'I am a believer if Allah wills' because it implies doubt about faith, and he grounds this in the fact that action is not part of faith and that faith must be certain.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'I am a believer, if Allah wills,' do you ever do so to mask a secret doubt about your own faith? What would it mean for you to drop that 'if' and affirm your faith with absolute certainty?
?
How often do you tie your identity as a believer to your actions—your prayers, your charity, your daily conduct? How does Maturidi's separation of action from faith challenge the way you evaluate your own faith? Are you willing to accept that your faith can be complete even when your actions fall short?
?
If you were to answer the question 'Are you a believer?' right now, without any hesitation or qualification, would your heart respond with full conviction? If not, what is the source of that hesitation? Write one specific step you can take today to strengthen the certainty of your faith.

The Reality of Islam and Iman: One True Religion
Author argues that Islam and Iman are identical in reality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's argument that the true reality of Islam and Iman is identical, despite apparent differences in outward expressions.

Core Idea
Islam and Iman share one reality as the religion itself.

This passage from Imam Maturidi's Kitab al-Tawhid addresses a key theological question: are Islam and Iman (faith) the same or different? The author argues that while they may appear distinct in outward manifestations, their true essence is one. He cites Quranic evidence and concludes that the names refer to a single reality. Let's explore his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the author's opening statement about the true reality of Islam.
The Arabic contains OCR uncertainties; read the translation alongside for clarity.
2
Identify the author's main claim
The author states that the reality of submission (Islam) is the religion itself, not just outward appearances. Locate this claim in the text.
Look for the phrase 'حقيقته فهو الدين في الحقيقة'
3
Examine the Quranic support
The author references Quranic verses to argue that those who manifest Islam outwardly but lack true faith are rebuked. Find the reference to 'If you are truthful' and the verse about disbelieving after belief.
The exact verses are not fully clear due to OCR, but the argument is that outward Islam alone is insufficient.
4
Understand the conclusion
The author concludes that the names 'Islam' and 'Iman' indicate one reality. Reflect on how this answers the question of their relationship.
The passage ends with a prayer, but the doctrinal point is complete.

والاستسلام واما حقيقته فهو الدين في الحقيقة لا ما ذكر من الظواهر دليل ذلك الامر الذي ذكروا ان الله قال في اخر السوو[؟] عليك أن أسلمو[؟] لا تمنوا علي السلطة حكم ولو كان الاسلام ما اظهروا فقد كان ذلك كيف قال ان كنتم صادقين ثم فيه اثر جعلهم مسلمین كا[؟] نك دنیا فلن تقبل مند تم [؟] قالوا ان هل وا للإيمان لاما أظهرو [؟] ان الايمان هو الاسطور وكذلك بالون مع غير الاسلام كيف يهدي الله قوما كفروا بعد إيمانهم الآية [؟] ذلك لاعتبار [؟] الذي الذي هو الاسلام به غير الإيمان الذي وصف ثم جعلهم مبدل دين الإسلام بالكفر بعد الايمان ليعلموا انها واحد معما كان فيما [؟] من قوله قولوا آمنا بالله وما أنزل علينا [؟] مسلمين والأصل عندنا أن الأسماء انما جعلت المعرفة [؟] فيما أريد [؟] بامور جعل [؟] و عليهم وفيما وعدوا واوعدها [؟] لم يكن اخذ غير [؟] جري ان الذكر باسم الإيما او الاسكة [؟] و [؟] دين الانظار [؟] من حيث الاسم ثبت ان حقيقتها واحد وان [؟] التفريق أنها من بعيد [؟] ولا قوة الا بالله تعالي وصلى الله على سيدنا محمد راله العطر الطاهرين

Had Islam been what they manifested, then that would have been so. He said: 'If you are truthful'? Then there is the effect of making them Muslims...? in this world, then it will not be accepted from you. Then He made them exchangers of the religion of Islam for disbelief after faith, so that they might know that they are one...? from His saying: 'Say: We believe in Allah and what has been revealed to us'...? Muslims. And the principle with us is that names are only made for knowledge of their people...? in what is intended...? with matters of Islam...? and upon them...? and in what they were promised and threatened...? then it was not taken otherwise...? runs that the mention by the name of faith or Islam...? and...? of the religion of...? restricting the mention of it from the aspect of the name established that their reality is one...? and the difference...? that it is from far...? And there is no power except with Allah, the Exalted. And may Allah bless our master Muhammad and his pure and good family.

Commentary
This passage is a theological discussion on the relationship between Islam and Iman (faith). The author argues that the true reality of submission (Islam) is the religion itself, not merely outward manifestations. He cites Quranic verses to support this, noting that Allah reproaches those who claim to have submitted but are not truthful, and that He made those who exchanged Islam for disbelief after faith an example. The conclusion is that the names 'Islam' and 'Iman' refer to the same reality, though they may be distinguished in some contexts. The passage ends with a prayer.

?

?

?
The author argues that the reality of religion is one, not fragmented. Are you living as if your faith and your daily life are separate compartments? If not, what step can you take to integrate your beliefs into every aspect of your day, starting right now?

Refutation of Exclusive Good and Evil from Light and Darkness
Maturidi refutes the dualist claim using a murder confession example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi refutes the dualist claim that only good comes from light and only evil from darkness using the example of a murderer's confession.

Core Idea
Good and evil can come from the same being, refuting dualist exclusivity.

The dualists claim that light produces only good and darkness only evil. Maturidi presents a simple counterexample: a man kills (evil) and then confesses truthfully (good). This shows that both good and evil can emanate from the same agent, undermining the core dualist premise.

Guided Path
1
Read the pasage carefully
Read the Arabic passage from 'وعورضوا بقولهم' to 'وهو تَرْك القتل'. Then read the translation. Notice how Maturidi structures the refutation.
2
Identify the dualist claim and the counterexample
The dualists claim that light does only good and darkness only evil. Identify the two scenarios of the murder confession and see how each shows both good and evil from the same person.
The key is that the same being produces both good and evil acts.
3
Reflect on the logical force
Ask yourself: why does this example refute the dualist claim? Because it shows that the source of good and evil is not inherently tied to light or darkness, but to the agent's choices.
This refutation does not rely on theology but on observable human actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعورضوا بقولهم لا يكون من النور غير الخير ولا من الظلمة غير الشر: فإذا قتل رجل ثم أقرّ ، فإن كان المقرّ هو الذي قتل، وهو صدق، فقد عمل به الخير بعد الشر. وإن كان المقرّ هو الذي لم يقتل، فهو كذب، وهو شر ، فقد كان منه الخير ، وهو تَرْك القتل. وكذلك من قولهم : إن كل حاسة لا تدرك ما تدركه الأخرى. ثم فيها سمع قال: سمعت، أو فيما رأى قال: رأيت وما قال به رأيت وسمعت غير الذي به سمع ورأى. وذلك جواب ادعاء الإدراك بما لا يدرك.
And they are opposed by their statement: 'Nothing but good comes from light and nothing but evil from darkness.' For if a man kills and then confesses, if the one who confesses is the one who killed, and it is truth, then good has been done (i.e., confessing truth) after evil. And if the one who confesses is not the one who killed, it is falsehood, and it is evil, then good has come from him, namely refraining from killing. And similarly from their statement: 'Each sense does not perceive what the other perceives.' Then, in it, the one who hears said: 'I heard,' or in what he saw he said: 'I saw,' and he does not say 'I saw and heard' with the same [organ] by which he heard and saw. And that is a response to their claim of perception of what is not perceived.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage refutes two dualist claims. The first is that light produces only good and darkness only evil. Maturidi presents a counterexample: a man kills (evil) and then confesses (good act of truthfulness). This shows that both good and evil can emanate from the same being, undermining the exclusive assignment. Furthermore, if the man did not kill but confessed falsely, that is evil, but the act of not killing (refraining from evil) is good—so again both good and evil are possible from one source. The second claim is about the senses: each sense perceives only its own domain. Maturidi argues that when a person says 'I heard' or 'I saw,' they do not claim to hear with the eyes or see with the ears. This indicates that each sense has its proper object, which is obvious. The response is directed against the dualists' attempt to draw an analogy with light and darkness.

Key Terms
خير
شر
إقرار
صدق
كذب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Light does only good and darkness only evil, and these moral qualities are exclusive to their respective sources.
Correction: The murder example shows that good and evil can come from the same being, so moral qualities are not exclusive to light or darkness.

Checkpoint
In the murder example, what demonstrates that both good and evil can come from the same being?
A) The confessor tells the truth after killing.
B) The confessor lies about not killing.
C) Both A and B.
D) Neither.

Key Takeaway
The murder confession example shows that good and evil can coexist in the same agent, refuting the dualist claim of exclusive moral sources.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Can you recall a time when you attributed your good deed to your own effort and your bad deed to circumstances or someone else? How does Maturidi's refutation of dualism challenge you to take full responsibility for both your virtues and your sins? What will you change in how you account for your actions starting today?
?
In what areas of your life do you unconsciously separate your good and evil actions as if they come from different 'sources' within you? How would your self-accountability improve if you acknowledged that both arise from the same soul? Write down one specific area you will confront.
?
This lesson shows that truthful confession after murder is good, and false confession while refraining from murder is also good in a limited sense. Are there situations where you have lied to avoid a greater evil? How will you ensure your moral choices are consistent and sincere before Allah, not self-justifying?

Refutation of the Sense Perception Analogy
Maturidi refutes the dualist analogy based on sense perception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's response to the dualist analogy that each sense perceives only its own object, and why this analogy fails to prove exclusive moral sources.

Core Idea
Each sense has its proper object, but this does not imply exclusivity of moral sources.

The dualists draw an analogy: just as each sense perceives only its own domain (sight sees only colors, hearing only sounds), so light does only good and darkness only evil. Maturidi points out that this analogy is flawed because it does not necessitate exclusive moral sources; it merely shows diversity of perception, not that a single being cannot produce both good and evil.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on senses
Read the Arabic from 'وكذلك من قولهم' to the end. Then read the translation. Understand the dualist analogy and Maturidi's response.
2
Analyze the analogy
The dualists claim that just as each sense has its own object and cannot perceive others, so light and darkness produce only their respective moral qualities. Identify how Maturidi counters this: by noting that when we say 'I heard' or 'I saw', we never claim to hear with the eyes or see with the ears, which is obvious. This shows that the analogy does not prove that a single being cannot produce both good and evil.
The response is that the analogy simply describes diversity, not exclusivity.
3
Connect to the main refutation
Ask yourself: why does this analogy fail to support the dualist claim? Because it does not show that the same being cannot produce both good and evil; it only says that each sense has a specific function, which is uncontroversial.
The real issue is whether moral qualities are tied to specific cosmic sources, and the sense analogy does not address that.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعورضوا بقولهم لا يكون من النور غير الخير ولا من الظلمة غير الشر: فإذا قتل رجل ثم أقرّ ، فإن كان المقرّ هو الذي قتل، وهو صدق، فقد عمل به الخير بعد الشر. وإن كان المقرّ هو الذي لم يقتل، فهو كذب، وهو شر ، فقد كان منه الخير ، وهو تَرْك القتل. وكذلك من قولهم : إن كل حاسة لا تدرك ما تدركه الأخرى. ثم فيها سمع قال: سمعت، أو فيما رأى قال: رأيت وما قال به رأيت وسمعت غير الذي به سمع ورأى. وذلك جواب ادعاء الإدراك بما لا يدرك.
And they are opposed by their statement: 'Nothing but good comes from light and nothing but evil from darkness.' For if a man kills and then confesses, if the one who confesses is the one who killed, and it is truth, then good has been done (i.e., confessing truth) after evil. And if the one who confesses is not the one who killed, it is falsehood, and it is evil, then good has come from him, namely refraining from killing. And similarly from their statement: 'Each sense does not perceive what the other perceives.' Then, in it, the one who hears said: 'I heard,' or in what he saw he said: 'I saw,' and he does not say 'I saw and heard' with the same [organ] by which he heard and saw. And that is a response to their claim of perception of what is not perceived.

Commentary
This passage refutes two dualist claims. The first is that light produces only good and darkness only evil. Maturidi presents a counterexample: a man kills (evil) and then confesses (good act of truthfulness). This shows that both good and evil can emanate from the same being, undermining the exclusive assignment. Furthermore, if the man did not kill but confessed falsely, that is evil, but the act of not killing (refraining from evil) is good—so again both good and evil are possible from one source. The second claim is about the senses: each sense perceives only its own domain. Maturidi argues that when a person says 'I heard' or 'I saw,' they do not claim to hear with the eyes or see with the ears. This indicates that each sense has its proper object, which is obvious. The response is directed against the dualists' attempt to draw an analogy with light and darkness.

Correction: The analogy only shows that each sense has a specific function, not that a single being cannot produce both good and evil.

What is Maturidi's response to the dualist sense perception analogy?
A) He denies that each sense has its own object.
B) He affirms that each sense has its own object but argues this does not prove exclusive moral sources.

D) He uses the analogy to prove that light and darkness are not exclusive.

Key Takeaway
The sense perception analogy does not prove that moral qualities are exclusive to light or darkness; it only shows diversity of perception.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a time when you were absolutely certain about a moral or religious truth based on a simple analogy. Did you ever question whether that analogy actually holds? If not, what might you be afraid to discover if you examined it?
?
The dualists claimed to perceive something that cannot be perceived—exclusivity of moral sources. Is there a belief you hold that you treat as self-evident, but upon reflection, you have no direct evidence for? Will you honestly examine that belief today?
?
Maturidi uses everyday language—the way we talk about seeing and hearing—to refute a complex argument. Where in your own life have you ignored simple, clear facts because you were drawn to an elegant but false theory? What would it cost you to let go of that theory?

The Denier's Dilemma: Belief or Denial?
Al-Maturidi challenges the denier with a dilemma about belief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Maturidi uses a simple question about belief to expose the self-defeating nature of denying prophethood.

Core Idea
Denying all belief makes denial itself baseless.

In this passage, Imam al-Maturidi engages a hypothetical denier of prophethood. Instead of presenting proofs directly, he first forces the denier to clarify his own epistemic stance. By asking whether the denier believes anything at all, al-Maturidi sets a trap that reveals the inconsistency of absolute denial. The denier's answer, whether affirmative or negative, leads to a collapse of his position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its translation. Notice that al-Maturidi poses a single question and then explores two possible answers. Pay attention to the logical consequences he draws from each.
The passage uses a dialectical style common in Islamic theology.
2
Examine the first answer: 'No'
If the denier says he believes nothing, he admits he does not even believe his own denial or his own existence. This undercuts any objection he might raise against prophethood.
Al-Maturidi dismisses the denier's efforts as 'mistaken'.
3
Examine the second answer: 'Yes'
If the denier says he does believe something, al-Maturidi points out that the denier's own belief could be false, as many beliefs have proven false. Moreover, there might be a pure nature that perceives truth, so the denier cannot rule out true belief.
The denier's position reduces to uncertainty and ignorance.
4
Understand the conclusion
Al-Maturidi concludes that the denier, by either answer, becomes a total skeptic who cannot affirm or deny anything with certainty. This shows the futility of denying prophethood without a consistent epistemic basis.
The principle: whoever abandons knowledge and speaks without basis invalidates all assertion and negation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال له : تعتقد شيئًا ألبتة ؟ فإن قال : لا ، أقر أنه لم يعتقد تكذيب من ذكر ، ولا أنه هو، ولا هو حي أو ميت، فتكلّفه الأجوبة والمعارضات خطأ. وإن قال: نعم، قيل: لعلك تعتقده بما لم تبلغ قوة دَرْكك وعلمك بالأشياء مبلغ الإحالة؛ إذ قد رأيت كثيرًا من المعتقدين بطل اعتقادهم ، فلعل طبيعتك أرتك ذلك الفساد؛ ويجوز أن تكون في الطبائع طبيعة نقيةٌ تُدرك كذلك فيما اعتقدت؛ ويظهر جهلك [بعد]. فمهما قال من شيء فهو له ـ في جميع ما أنكر - جواب. وأصله أن كل من استحار الخروج من المعارف والتفوه بغير الموجود في الطبائع بلا شيء سوى / أنه لم يكن أو لعله يكون أبطل سبيل تثبيت شيء ألبتة أو نفيه، ويكون في حد الشاكين في البيان كله ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Then it is said to him: ‘Do you believe anything at all?’ If he says: ‘No,’ he admits that he does not believe in the denial of those mentioned, nor that he himself is alive or dead, so his effort at answers and objections is mistaken. And if he says: ‘Yes,’ it is said: ‘Perhaps you believe it by something that does not reach the strength of your perception and your knowledge of things to the extent of impossibility; since you have seen many believers whose belief turned out false, perhaps your nature showed you that corruption; and it is possible that among natures there is a pure nature that perceives correctly in what you believe; and your ignorance appears [later]. So whatever he says of something, it is for him – in all that he denies – an answer. And the principle is that whoever is bewildered in exiting from knowledges and uttering what is not present in natures without anything except that it was not or perhaps it will be, has invalidated the way of establishing anything at all or negating it, and he is among the doubters in all discourse, and there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical challenge to the denier of prophethood. Al-Maturidi asks the denier whether he believes anything at all. If he says no, he admits that even his own denial is not believed, and his entire argument collapses. If he says yes, then he is asked whether his belief is based on something that does not reach certainty – and since he has seen many false beliefs, perhaps his own belief is also false. Moreover, there might exist a pure nature that perceives truth, so the denier cannot rule out the possibility of true belief. Thus, whatever the denier says can be turned against him, and his position reduces to total skepticism, which invalidates any assertion or denial. This shows that the denier is ultimately a doubter in all matters.

Key Terms
اعتقاد
طبائع
شك
إحالة
جهل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The denier of prophethood has a coherent and consistent position.
Correction: Al-Maturidi shows that the denier must either admit to not believing anything (which undermines his own denial) or admit to believing something (which opens his belief to doubt and uncertainty, leading to total skepticism). Thus, his position is incoherent.

Checkpoint
What is the consequence if the denier says he does not believe anything?
A) He is considered a true skeptic.
B) He admits that he does not even believe his own denial, so his objections are baseless.
C) He must provide a proof for his position.
D) He is excused from further argument.

Key Takeaway
Denying all belief leads to self-refuting skepticism, while affirming belief exposes uncertainty, making the denier's position indefensible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a doubt about your faith, do you tend to avoid taking a stand, thinking 'maybe' or 'I don't know'? How does al-Maturidi's dilemma expose the danger of such avoidance? What is one belief you have been avoiding examining, and what would it cost you to settle it today?
?
If someone asked you the same question—'Do you believe anything at all?'—would you answer with certainty, or would you hesitate? What does your hesitation reveal about the foundation of your faith? Commit to one action you will take this week to strengthen that foundation.
?
The passage warns that those who rely on 'it was not or perhaps it will be' invalidate establishing anything. In what areas of your life have you allowed mere possibilities to keep you from conviction? Will you continue to let 'perhaps' rule your heart, or will you seek the knowledge that leads to certainty?

5 min
The Common Saying That Only God Creates
Maturidi uses a universal confession to refute human creation of actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi uses the universal Muslim confession that only Allah creates to prove that human actions are not created by humans.

Core Idea
Attributing creation to humans contradicts the core Muslim belief that only Allah creates.

Imam Maturidi presents a concise argument grounded in the everyday Muslim declaration that there is no creator but Allah. He shows that if we claim humans originate their own actions, we would be assigning the divine attribute of creation to them, leading to a contradiction of tawhid. This lesson unpacks that logical proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the conditional structure: 'if we were to make... then we would have attributed...'.
The argument is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the foundational belief
Maturidi begins with the common saying: 'there is no creator other than Allah and no lord besides Him'. This is the premise everyone agrees on.
This is a universally accepted statement among Muslims.
3
Trace the conditional argument
He then says: if we attribute the coming into being of actions (their emergence from non-existence) to humans, we are giving them the attribute of creation. That would imply a creator other than Allah.
The logic is: origination from non-existence is the meaning of 'creation'.
4
Understand the conclusion
Such a view is contradictory to the first principle and also implies that a human could be called 'lord' of his own action. Maturidi rejects this as absurd.
The argument is a reductio ad absurdum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضاً القول المتعارف في الخلق أن لا خالق غير الله ولا رب سواه، ولو جعلنا حدث الأفعال وخروجها من العدم إلى الوجود، ثم فناءها بعد الوجود، ثم خروجها على تقدير من اربابها لجعلنا لها وصف الخلق الذي به صار الخلق خلقا، وفي ذلك لزوم القول بخالق سواه، وفي جوازه مناقضة قول من ذكرت مع ما لو جاز ذلك لجاز القول برب فعله، وذلك مدفوع. وبالله التوفيق.
And also, the common saying among creation is that there is no creator other than Allah and no lord besides Him. And if we were to make the coming into being of actions and their emergence from non-existence into existence, then their annihilation after existence, then their emergence according to the estimation of their owners, we would have attributed to them the description of creation (khalq) by which the creation became creation. In that is the necessity of affirming a creator other than Him, and in its permissibility is a contradiction to the saying of those I mentioned; moreover, if that were permissible, it would be permissible to affirm a lord of his own action. And that is repudiated. And with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This proof appeals to the universal Muslim confession that there is no creator but Allah. Maturidi argues that if we attribute the actual origination (ḥudūth) of actions – their coming from non-existence, their existence, and their passing away – to the human agents, then we are assigning the attribute of creation to them. This would imply a creator besides Allah, contradicting the fundamental belief. It would also allow the claim that a human is the 'lord' of his own action, which is absurd. Therefore, the view that humans create their own actions is rejected.

Key Terms
خالق (creator)
رب (lord)
خلق (creation)
حدث (coming into being)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'creation' can be metaphorically applied to human actions without theological consequences.
Correction: Maturidi insists that the origination of actions from non-existence is the same as creation, so applying it to humans leads to associating partners with God (shirk).

Checkpoint
What does attributing the origination of actions to humans imply?
A) It affirms divine oneness
B) It necessitates a creator other than Allah
C) It is a valid interpretation
D) It strengthens faith

Key Takeaway
Maturidi's argument shows that affirming human creation of actions contradicts the fundamental Islamic declaration that only Allah creates.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'Allah alone creates', do you truly believe that includes your every action, or do you secretly feel that you are the independent author of your deeds? How would your day change if you lived with the conviction that your Lord is the only Creator even of your choices?
?
Maturidi says that attributing creation to humans leads to 'affirming a lord of his own action.' Is there any area of your life where you act as if you are the lord of your own actions, deciding without reference to Allah? What would it cost you to hand over that perceived lordship?
?
The common Muslim saying 'no creator but Allah' is on your tongue. But does your heart tremble when you realize that even your ability to say it is created? If you truly believed that, would you still fear anyone or anything other than Him? What is one fear you can surrender today because only Allah creates outcomes?

Knowledge of the Acquired Action and Refutation of Mu'tazilites
Maturidi refutes Mu'tazilite view on knowledge of acquired action using Quran 23:91.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that the acquired action is known only through knowledge of God, and how he refutes the Mu'tazilite position using Quran 23:91.

Core Idea
The acquired action cannot be known independently; it is known through God.

In this lesson, we explore Imam Maturidi's discussion on whether the acquired action (al-muktasab) can be known independently. He argues that it is only known through knowledge of God, and refutes the Mu'tazilite interpretation that leads to perpetual doubt. The Quranic verse 23:91 is used to highlight the error.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage about the objection regarding the acquired action. Focus on the structure: the objection, Maturidi's response, and the Quranic verse.
Notice how Maturidi shifts the discussion from knowing the acquired action to knowing God.
2
Identify the Mu'tazilite position
Understand that Mu'tazilites make knowledge of the acquired action impossible, leading to perpetual doubt. Maturidi links this to the negation of any other god with Allah.
The Quranic verse 'Each god would have taken away what he created' is key.
3
Reflect on the consequence
Ask yourself: why does Maturidi consider denying or affirming things about God as unbelief? How does this connect to the acquired action?
This reinforces the idea that all knowledge of creation is tied to knowledge of the Creator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم عارض : هل يُعرف به المكتسب من غيره ؟ قال الشيخ رحمه الله : وهي المعارضة إن اشتبه المكتسب لغيره حتى لا يُعرف حقيقة واحد منهما وكان قد ثبت أنهما مخلوقان معا لذلك. وبعد، فإنه ليس على معرفة المكتسب وإنما هو على معرفة ما الله، لا عرفه في خلقه. لا أنفي عنه ما هو له، ولا أثبت له ما ليس له فأكون كاذبًا عليه، وذلك كفر. وعلى قول المعتزلة لا وجه لمعرفته، فيحصل أبدا على الشك، ولا يصل إليه؛ وذلك هو المعنى الذي نفي الله أن يكون معه إله، حققه أهل الاعتزال سفها بغير علم، وذلك في قوله : ﴿إذا لذهب كل إله بما خلق﴾ [المؤمنون، 23:91]. والله الموفق. ثم فبلغ قوله : إنه لا يُعلم بنفس الحركة أنها مخلوقة؛ فيجب هذا في كل عرض نحو الجمع والتفريق، فيبطل أن يكون في شيء من ذلك دلالة خلقه. ثم لا سبيل إلى معرفة حقيقة الأعيان بدونها. فكأن الله لم يُقم دلالة على خلقه بكون تلك بالله دون خلقه أبدا. وذلك قول لم يتوهمه الشيطان، لعله أن أحدا من أوليائه يبلغ بطاعته إياه هذا المبلغ. نسأل الله العصمة ذلك. وعلى قوله إن الشيء لا يدل على الله، إنما يدل - إذا علم سببه - إسقاطه الدلالة عن الأجسام من أن يُعرف بها الله سبحانه. قال : ومن عظيم ما أجمعوا عليه أن دليل خلق الجسم حدثه، فكذلك كل محدث يدفع إلى هذا. وسأل الدليل، وأيد ذلك بما يجوز أن يعرفه محدثًا من لا يعرف خلقا. قال الفقيه رحمه الله : نقول وبالله التوفيق: أهل التوحيد إنما تكلموا في حدث العالم وثبات محدثه، ولا أحد تكلف القول بخلق العالم وثبات خالقه. فلولا أنهم رأوا بالأول كفاية عن الثاني، وجعلوا ثبات الحدث دليلاً مقنعا في الخلق، لصنعوا مثله؛ لأن لكل إليه حاجة، وذلك ممتنع. وقد احتج بخلق القرآن بالتبعض والتجزئة، فمثله في كل الأعراض قائم، فيلزم القول به. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Then he objected: Is the acquired action known from other than it? The Shaykh, may God have mercy on him, said: The objection is: if the acquired action is ambiguous with other than it so that the reality of neither is known, yet it has been established that both are created together for that reason. Moreover, it is not about knowing the acquired action; rather it is about knowing what God [is], not what He has recognized in His creation. I do not deny what is His, nor do I affirm for Him what is not His, lest I be a liar about Him, and that is unbelief. According to the Mu'tazilites, there is no way to know it, so one always remains in doubt and never attains it. That is the meaning of God's negation that there be with Him any god, which the people of I'tizal actualized foolishly without knowledge, in His saying: 'Each god would have taken away what he created' (23:91). And God is the Grantor of success. Then his statement reached [us]: It is not known by the motion itself that it is created; so this applies to every accident like combination and separation, thus nullifying that any of that is a sign of His creation. Then there is no way to know the reality of entities without them. It is as if God never established any indication of His creation by those [accidents] being through God without His creation ever. That is a saying that even Satan did not imagine; perhaps one of his allies reaches this level through his obedience to him. We ask God for protection from that. And according to his saying that a thing does not indicate God; rather it indicates—if its cause is known—the dropping of indication from bodies that God be known through them. He said: Among the greatest things they agreed upon is that the proof of the creation of a body is its temporality; so likewise every temporal thing pushes to that. He asked for the proof and supported that with [the claim] that one who does not know creation can know it as temporal. The Faqih, may God have mercy on him, said: We say, and with God is success: The people of Tawhid only spoke about the temporality of the world and the establishment of its Originator, and no one undertook to speak about the creation of the world and the establishment of its Creator. For if they had not seen sufficiency in the first over the second, and made the establishment of temporality a convincing proof in creation, they would have done the like; because everyone has a need of it, and that is impossible. And he argued by the creation of the Qur'an through partition and division, so the like of that stands in all accidents, necessitating the affirmation of it. There is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage combines two related teachings: first, the nature of knowledge of the acquired action (المكتسب) and a refutation of the Mu'tazilite interpretation of Quran 23:91; second, a broader argument about the proof of creation. Maturidi states that the acquired action is known not independently but through knowledge of God. Denying what belongs to God or affirming what does not is unbelief. The Mu'tazilites, by making knowledge of the acquired action impossible, fall into perpetual doubt, contradicting the Quranic verse that implies each god would take his creation away. Then Maturidi critiques the view that motion itself does not indicate creation, extending it to all accidents, which would destroy all signs of creation. He argues that the people of Tawhid correctly use the temporality of the world as a proof for its Creator, without needing additional proofs for each detail. The passage ends by rejecting the argument from the creation of the Qur'an via partition, stating that such reasoning would apply to all accidents.

Key Terms
المكتسب
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the acquired action can be known independently of God.
Correction: Maturidi insists that the acquired action is only known through knowledge of God; trying to know it independently leads to doubt and error.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi say is the consequence of the Mu'tazilite position on the knowledge of the acquired action?
A) It leads to certainty.
B) It leads to perpetual doubt.
C) It confirms the Quranic verse.
D) It establishes the creation of the world.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi insists that knowledge of the acquired action is inseparable from knowledge of God, and the Mu'tazilite view leads to doubt contrary to Quranic teaching.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what specific area of your life do you tend to judge actions or outcomes without first grounding your understanding in who God is and His attributes? What step will you take today to connect that area to knowledge of God?
?
When you speak about God—whether to others or in your own thoughts—do you sometimes affirm things about Him without clear evidence from revelation? How will you ensure your speech about God is truthful and not akin to the disbelief mentioned in this passage?
?
The Mu'tazilite position leads to perpetual doubt about what is truly from God. Is there any aspect of your faith—such as divine decree or the nature of human actions—where you have been content with uncertainty instead of seeking certainty through God's words? What will you do to replace that doubt with firm belief?

Proof of Creation Through Temporality and Refutation of Alternative Arguments
Maturidi defends proof from temporality and refutes alternative views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that the temporality (huduth) of the world is a sufficient proof for its Creator, and his critique of the view that accidents do not indicate creation.

Core Idea
The temporality of bodies is the key proof for their creation.

In this lesson, we examine Maturidi's response to the claim that motion or accidents do not indicate creation. He argues that this would nullify all signs of creation and then affirms that the people of Tawhid correctly rely on the temporality of the world as proof. He also criticizes the argument from the creation of the Qur'an via partition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the motion claim
Read the part where it says motion itself does not indicate creation. Notice how Maturidi extends this to all accidents, which would destroy the proof of creation.
This is a reductio ad absurdum: if motion doesn't indicate creation, then nothing indicates creation.
2
Understand the positive argument
Maturidi states that the proof of a body's creation is its temporality (huduth). This is a foundational principle agreed upon by scholars of Tawhid.
The temporality of the world suffices; no need for extra proofs for each detail.
3
Examine the critique of the Qur'an creation argument
Maturidi rejects the argument from partition and division, showing it would apply to all accidents and lead to absurdity.
This criticism reinforces the sufficiency of the temporality proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
