They alleged generality, while they in fact made the threat (al-wa'īd) apply to one of the two groups of mankind, those who are not believers. There is no power except with Allah. Then it has been established by the proofs of the Qur'an, and what the people of faith hold, and what has proceeded from the tongue, that faith (al-īmān) is affirmation (al-taṣdīq); with it we believe, and by it the rulings of the Qur'an proceed in lawful and unlawful, and by it the acts of worship are established, and participation in congregations, and gathering in assemblies of remembrance and good deeds without mutual denial among them. Acceptance of the right of the believers, and likewise all that has proceeded in address; there is not found a Mu'tazilī, nor a Khārijī, nor a Ḥashwī — despite their containing types of sins and evil deeds which they know are major sins or which they do not know their reality — who permits in the matter of address that he himself be other than one who has what is in it [of the status]. So it stands established that faith does not leave him and that the name stands for him. Thus by this statement — whoever rejects it is known to be an obstinate antagonist — what the Khawārij and Mu'tazila said is invalidated. There is no power except with Allah. And also, Allah the Exalted preserved for him the name of faith along with the realization of what the threat entails in His judgment by His saying: 'O you who have believed, why do you say what you do not do?' [al-Ṣaff 61:2-3]. So He made anger [arise] against him with the name of faith by the word of rebuke that does not permit utterance before the commission of the sin by His saying: 'Why do you say?' And anger does not necessitate the sin for which, in wisdom, forgiveness becomes necessary. And He said: 'And if two factions among the believers fight' [al-Ḥujurāt 49:9]. He affirmed for them the name of faith while imposing the name of aggression (al-baghy) on one of them in fighting, and obligated those present to assist the wronged one until the other returns to the command of Allah. And if that had been an exit from faith, the truth in such a case would be other than what was mentioned. And He said: 'O you who have believed, prescribed for you is legal retribution in cases of murder' [al-Baqarah 2:178]. And it is known that it is only obligatory for intentional killing. So He affirmed for them at the beginning of the verse the name of faith, and preserved brotherhood between them, and informed that that is a lightening from your Lord and mercy. And these descriptions would be far from those whose action excludes them from faith. And He said: 'And those who believed and did not emigrate — you have no guardianship of them in anything' [al-Anfāl 8:72], then He said: 'But if they seek help from you in the religion' — the verse. He affirmed for them the name of faith and united them in religion despite their failure to emigrate, along with the greatness of the threat in it by His saying: 'Those whom the angels take in death while they are wronging themselves' [al-Nisā' 4:97] — the verse. And He said: 'O you who have believed, do not take My enemy and your enemy as allies' [al-Mumtaḥanah 60:1] — the verse. And He also said: 'Do not betray Allah and the Messenger' [al-Anfāl 8:27] — the verse. So He affirmed for them the name of faith despite the evil of their deed. There is no power except with Allah. And also, Allah the Exalted said: 'O you who have believed, repent to Allah with sincere repentance' [al-Taḥrīm 66:8], and said: 'And repent to Allah, all of you, O believers' [al-Nūr 24:31]. He informed that they have sins that are forgiven by repentance and expiated while preserving the name of faith. And according to the saying of these [opponents], that is not permissible. So it stands established that the true saying is the saying of those who...
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage is a proof that the name of faith (īmān) remains with Muslims even when they commit major sins, refuting the Khawārij and Mu'tazila who held that grave sinners are no longer believers. The author begins by noting that the opponents (Khawārij/Mu'tazila) wrongly confine the threat of punishment to one group—non-believers—while they themselves agree that the term 'believer' is used for sinners in the Qur'anic address. He then establishes that the definition of faith is affirmation (taṣdīq), and that the Qur'anic rulings and communal practices are based on this. No sect denies that a sinner can be called a believer in Qur'anic discourse; even the Khawārij and Mu'tazila admit this in practice, though they theoretically deny it. Therefore, the claim that sin removes the name of faith is invalid. Next, Maturidi presents a series of Qur'anic verses that address sinners as 'O you who have believed' and yet rebuke or command them: 1) Sūrat al-Ṣaff 61:2-3 rebukes believers for saying what they do not do, yet they are called believers; the anger (maqt) mentioned does not necessitate that sin removes faith. 2) Sūrat al-Ḥujurāt 49:9 speaks of two parties of believers fighting, one being aggressors; they remain believers despite the aggression. If fighting removed faith, the ruling would be different. 3) Sūrat al-Baqarah 2:178 prescribes retribution for murder, addressing the believers; intentional killing is a major sin, but they are addressed as believers, and brotherhood is preserved. 4) Sūrat al-Anfāl 8:72 addresses believers who did not emigrate, with a threat for those who die in that state; yet they are still called believers. 5) Sūrat al-Mumtaḥanah 60:1 forbids taking enemies as allies, addressing believers who might commit this sin. 6) Sūrat al-Anfāl 8:27 forbids betraying Allah and the Messenger, again addressing believers. 7) Sūrat al-Taḥrīm 66:8 and Sūrat al-Nūr 24:31 command repentance to believers, implying they have sins that are forgiven while they retain the name of faith. In all these cases, the Qur'an affirms the name of faith despite the presence of sins, proving that sin does not remove one from faith. The conclusion is that the correct position is what the author's school holds: the name of faith remains with the sinner, contrary to the Khawārij and Mu'tazila.

Key Terms
وعيد
مقت
بغي
هجرة
توبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That committing a major sin like murder or fighting removes a person from faith.
Correction: The Quranic verses show that people who commit such sins are still called believers and addressed by Allah.

Checkpoint
Which verse does Maturidi use to argue that even intentional killing does not remove the name of faith?
A) 'O you who have believed, why do you say what you do not do?'
B) 'And if two factions among the believers fight'
C) 'O you who have believed, prescribed for you is legal retribution in cases of murder'
D) 'O you who have believed, do not take My enemy and your enemy as allies'

Key Takeaway
Allah's address 'O you who have believed' to sinners proves that major sins do not remove the name of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a major sin, do you feel that your faith is completely gone, or do you still consider yourself a believer? How does the Qur'an's address 'O you who have believed' to sinners challenge your self-perception? Will you let this truth reshape how you view yourself after falling into sin?
?
This lesson shows that Allah preserves the name of faith for believers even when they sin. Is there a Muslim you have written off as a 'lost cause' because of their sins? How should this lesson change your treatment of them? What step will you take this week to show them the brotherhood of faith?
?
If you struggle with severe guilt after sinning, do you believe that repentance is still accepted because you remain a believer? Or do you feel unworthy to repent? How can the fact that Allah commands believers to repent—while still calling them believers—give you confidence to turn back to Him today?

The Retaliation Verse Proves Faith Remains
Maturidi cites the retaliation verse to show that even murderers are addressed as believers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Maturidi uses the Quranic verse on retaliation to argue that major sinners remain believers despite committing grave sins.

Core Idea
Even murderers are addressed as believers in the Quran.

Imam al-Maturidi begins his proof by citing a verse that prescribes retaliation for murder. Although murder is a major sin, the Quran addresses the perpetrators as 'O you who have believed.' Maturidi points out that the verse also calls them brothers and describes the law as a mercy—attributes that would be inappropriate if the sinners had lost their faith. This verse becomes a cornerstone of his argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation of the first part of Maturidi's argument, focusing on the verse about retaliation.
Notice how Maturidi highlights the address 'O you who have believed'.
2
Identify the key elements
Identify the verse, the sin (murder), the address (believers), and the additional descriptions (brothers, mercy).
Maturidi uses these to show that faith is not removed.
3
Reflect on the logical argument
Ask yourself: Why would it be inconsistent to call murderers believers if major sins expel faith? Maturidi argues that the Quran itself contradicts that view.
This is a refutation of the Khawarij and Mu'tazila.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لكان الحق في مثل ذلك غير الذي ذكر. وقال: يا أيها الذين آمنوا كتب عليكم القصاص في القتلى . ومعلوم أنه لا يجب إلا بقتل العمد فأثبت لهم في ابتداء الآية اسم الإيمان، وأبقى بينهما الأخوة ، وأخبر أن ذلك تخفيف من ربكم ورحمة، وتبعد هذه الأوصاف فيمن أخرجهم الفعل من الإيمان. وقال: والذين آمنوا ولم يهاجروا ما لكم من ولايتهم من شيء ، ثم قال : وإن استنصروكم في الدين " الآية " ، أثبت لهم اسم الإيمان وجمع بينهم في الدين على تخلفهم عن الهجرة، مع عظم ما فيه من الوعيد بقوله: الذين توفاهم الملائكة ظالمي أنفسهم الآية ، وقال : يا أيها الذين آمنوا لا تتخذوا عدوى وعدوكم أولياء ) الآية"، وقال أيضا: لا تخونوا الله والرسول " الآية"، فأثبت هم اسم الإيمان مع قبح صنيعهم. ولا قوة إلا بالله . وأيضاً إن الله تعالى قال: يا أيها الذين آمنوا توبوا إلى الله توبة نصوحا " ، وقال : وتوبوا إلى الله جميعا أيها المؤمنون، أخبر أن عليهم ذنوبا تغفر بالتوبة ويكفّر بها على إبقاء اسم الإيمان، وفي قول هؤلاء لا يجوز ذلك. فثبت أن القول [الحق] هو قول من لم يُزِل عنهم اسم الإيمان. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
But the truth in such a matter is other than what was mentioned. And He said: 'O you who have believed, prescribed for you is retaliation in cases of murder.' And it is known that it is only obligatory for intentional killing, so He affirmed for them at the beginning of the verse the name of faith (al-iman), and maintained brotherhood between them, and informed that that is a lightening from your Lord and a mercy. And these attributes are far from those whom action expelled from faith. And He said: 'And those who believed and did not emigrate – for you there is no guardianship of them until they emigrate.' Then He said: 'And if they seek help from you in the religion' – the verse. He affirmed for them the name of faith and united them in the religion despite their failure to emigrate, with the severity of the warning in His saying: 'Those whom the angels take in death while wronging themselves' – the verse. And He said: 'O you who have believed, do not take My enemy and your enemy as allies' – the verse. And He also said: 'Do not betray Allah and the Messenger' – the verse. He affirmed for them the name of faith despite the ugliness of their deed. And there is no power except with Allah. Also, Allah Almighty said: 'O you who have believed, repent to Allah with sincere repentance,' and He said: 'And repent to Allah all together, O believers.' He informed that they have sins that are forgiven by repentance and expiated, while maintaining the name of faith. And according to the saying of these (opponents), that is not permissible. So it is established that the true saying is the saying of the one who does not remove the name of faith from them. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage is a proof from the Quran that those who commit major sins (kaba'ir) are still called believers (mu'minun). Imam al-Maturidi refutes the view of those (the Khawarij and Mu'tazila) who claim that major sins expel a person from faith. He begins by citing Quranic verses that address sinners with 'O you who have believed' (ya ayyuha alladhina amanu). The first verse is about retaliation (al-qisas) in cases of murder, which is only applicable for intentional killing. Despite the sin of murder, the verse addresses the perpetrators as believers and even calls them 'brothers' (ikhwa) and describes the law as a 'lightening and mercy.' Al-Maturidi argues that such descriptions would be inappropriate if the sinners were expelled from faith. He then cites the verse about those who believed but did not emigrate (hijra). Although they are threatened with severe punishment, they are still called believers and considered part of the religious community. He also cites verses forbidding taking enemies as allies and betraying Allah and the Messenger, again addressing the sinners as believers despite the heinous nature of their acts. Finally, he cites the command to repent sincerely, addressed to 'O you who have believed,' indicating that they have sins that require repentance, yet the name of faith remains. The conclusion is that the correct position is that the name of faith (ism al-iman) is not removed from those who commit major sins, contrary to the view of the opponents.

القصاص
الكبائر

Correction: Maturidi shows that the Quran itself addresses murderers as believers, indicating that faith remains despite the sin.

A) They are expelled from faith.
B) They remain believers.
C) They are hypocrites.
D) They are disbelievers.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic address 'O you who have believed' to murderers proves that the name of faith remains even after major sins.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
If you are too quick to judge others who commit major sins, how does this verse confront your attitude? Will you now see them as brothers in faith, even if they fall short?

Other Verses Affirm Faith Despite Sins
Maturidi cites verses on emigration, alliances, and betrayal to show that major sinners are still called believers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will see how Imam al-Maturidi uses verses about emigration, alliances, and betrayal to further prove that major sinners retain the name of faith.

Core Idea
Even those who fail to emigrate or commit betrayal are still called believers.

Maturidi continues his argument by citing several Quranic verses that address believers who have committed significant sins. The first is about those who believed but did not emigrate, who are threatened with severe punishment yet still called believers. Then he cites verses warning against taking enemies as allies and betraying Allah and the Messenger, again addressing the wrongdoers as 'O you who have believed.' These examples show that even grave disobedience does not remove the name of faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the passage
Read the Arabic and translation covering the verses about emigration, alliances, and betrayal.
Notice how each verse begins with 'O you who have believed' despite the sin.
2
Compare the sins
Note that each sin is different: failing to emigrate, allying with enemies, betraying the Prophet. All are major sins.
Maturidi uses multiple examples to strengthen his case.
3
Understand the implication
Ask: If major sins expelled faith, would the Quran still address these sinners as believers? Maturidi says no.
This is a cumulative argument.

Repentance Verses Confirm Faith Remains
Maturidi cites repentance verses to show that sinners are still believers, then states the conclusion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Maturidi uses the verses commanding repentance to conclude that major sinners retain the name of faith.

Core Idea
Sinners are commanded to repent as believers, not as disbelievers.

Imam al-Maturidi's final proofs come from verses that command repentance. The Quran says 'O you who have believed, repent to Allah with sincere repentance' and 'And repent to Allah all together, O believers.' These verses assume that those who are sinning are still believers, because they are addressed as such. If major sins expelled faith, the command would be to first become believers and then repent. Maturidi concludes that the correct view is that the name of faith is not removed from major sinners.

Guided Path
1
Read the final part of the passage
Read the Arabic and translation covering the repentance verses and conclusion.
Notice how the address 'O believers' is used even when commanding repentance.
2
Understand the logical implication
If major sins expelled faith, the Quran would not address sinners as believers when commanding repentance. Instead, it would call them to faith first.
This is a key refutation.
3
Appreciate the conclusion
Maturidi concludes that the truth is with those who do not remove the name of faith from major sinners. This is the Maturidi position.
This contrasts with Khawarij and Mu'tazila.

Imam al-Maturidi refutes the view of those (the Khawarij and Mu'tazila) who claim that major sins expel a person from faith. He begins by citing Quranic verses that address sinners with 'O you who have believed' (ya ayyuha alladhina amanu). The first verse is about retaliation (al-qisas) in cases of murder, which is only applicable for intentional killing. Despite the sin of murder, the verse addresses the perpetrators as believers and even calls them 'brothers' (ikhwa) and describes the law as a 'lightening and mercy.' Al-Maturidi argues that such descriptions would be inappropriate if the sinners were expelled from faith. He then cites the verse about those who believed but did not emigrate (hijra). Although they are threatened with severe punishment, they are still called believers and considered part of the religious community. He also cites verses forbidding taking enemies as allies and betraying Allah and the Messenger, again addressing the sinners as believers despite the heinous nature of their acts. Finally, he cites the command to repent sincerely, addressed to 'O you who have believed,' indicating that they have sins that require repentance, yet the name of faith remains. The conclusion is that the correct position is that the name of faith (ism al-iman) is not removed from those who commit major sins, contrary to the view of the opponents.

Key Terms
التوبة
اسم الإيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the final conclusion of Imam al-Maturidi based on the repentance verses?
A) Major sinners become disbelievers until they repent.
B) Major sinners remain believers but must repent.
C) Major sinners are hypocrites.
D) Major sinners are forgiven without repentance.

Key Takeaway
The Quran commands sinners to repent while addressing them as believers, proving that faith remains even before repentance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you fall into a major sin, do you truly believe you are still a believer in the sight of Allah? Or does the weight of your sin make you doubt your faith? How does this verse challenge you to see yourself as Allah sees you—still addressed as 'believer'? Commit today to repent sincerely, knowing your faith remains intact.
?
If the Quran commands you to repent while calling you a believer, does that make repentance easier or harder for you? Does it give you hope that you can return to Allah without losing your identity? Examine your heart: have you ever avoided repentance because you felt you had already lost your faith? Let this verse shatter that lie.
?
You are called a believer even when you sin. Does that encourage you to sin less or to despair less? What is one sin you have been struggling with that makes you feel like a hypocrite? Today, accept that your faith is still real and valid—then act on that by turning to Allah with sincere repentance.

The Second Proof: Acts of Worship and the Name of Faith
Al-Maturidi presents a second proof based on the obligation of worship under the name of faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Maturidi argues that major sinners remain believers because they participate in acts of worship obligated under the name of faith.

Core Idea
Acts of worship are linked to faith; sinners still perform them, so faith remains.

Imam al-Maturidi presents a second type of argument. He observes that Allah has obligated many acts of worship under the name of faith, and the knowledge of what is lawful and unlawful is often tied to the presence or absence of faith. Yet those who commit acts of sin are still included in these obligations alongside believers. This shows that the name of faith is not removed from them. Let's examine this argument closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the main claim
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Identify the central claim al-Maturidi is making about the name of faith.
2
Notice the link between 'ibadat and iman
Al-Maturidi argues that acts of worship are obligated under the name of faith. Observe how he uses this to show that sinners are included in these obligations.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
The conclusion is that the name of faith is not removed from sinners. Think about why this is significant in the debate with the Mu'tazila.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونوع آخر، أن الله تعالى أوجب كثيرًا من العبادات باسم الإيمان ، وجعل علم الحِل والحزمة في كثير من ذلك اسم الإيمان وزواله، ثم شارك [فيها] من أحدث أفعال الفسق مع الإيمان غيره. ثبت أن اسم الإيمان غير زائل عنهم . مع ما قد تقدم بيان ما له اسم الإيمان [قدر] ما يت ما يكفى ذا العقل عن الإطناب. ثم إجماع النقلة في إثبات الشفاعة وتوارث الأمة في الصلاة على جميع من مات من أهل القبلة والاستغفار لهم والترحم عليهم هو الدليل لمن أبت نفسه تكذيب الأخبار الصحاح ومخالفة أئمة الهدى. ولا قوة إلا بالله. ثم قول المعتزلة في تحقيق الإياس من روح الله مع نفيهم اسم الكفر، وقد قال الله تعالى: وإنه لا ييأس من روح الله إلا القوم الكافرون، قول متناقض، إذ الله جمع بين الكفر والإياس ؛ فمن أثبت أحدهما لزمه الآخر . فإذ ثبت عندنا وعندهم أنه ليس بكافر - إذ الكفر في العرف تكذيب، وصاحب الكبيرة بالتصديق في حالة يرجو عفوه ويخاف عذابه، ويعلم أن من أيأسه من رحمة ربه ضال جاهل بالله - ثبت أنه ليس بمكذب. وفي الحقيقة الكفر اسم للستر، وصاحبها لا يستر شيئًا من نعم ربه ولا ينكر حقه . فيبطل أن يكون كافرًا؛ فمثله الإيمان في العرف والسمع تصديق، ومعلوم أنه لم يكذب الله في شيء، ثبت انه مؤمن. والله الموفق. الحق أن يقال : جميع الخوارج والمعتزلة عند ارتكابهم الكبائر كفرة على قولهم، مستوجبون للخلود في النار، وغيرهم من أصناف منتحلي الإسلام ،لا ، لأوجه أحدها أنهم أجمعوا على من رحمة الله ، وذلك وصف الكفر بما ذكرت من الآية، وبقوله : والذين كفروا بآيات الله ولقائه أولئك يئسوا من رحمتي، فلزم الفريقين اسم
And another type: Allah Almighty obligated many acts of worship under the name of faith, and made knowledge of the lawful and the forbidden in many of that dependent on the name of faith and its removal. Then He included in them the one who commits acts of sin alongside faith. It is established that the name of faith is not removed from them, along with what has preceded in explanation of what belongs to the name of faith, enough to suffice the intelligent without verbosity. Then the consensus of the transmitters in affirming intercession (al-shafa'ah), and the continuous practice of the community in praying over all who die from the people of the qibla, and seeking forgiveness for them, and asking mercy for them – this is the evidence for one whose soul refuses to deny the authentic reports and to oppose the guiding imams. And there is no power except with Allah. Then the saying of the Mu'tazila about the realization of despair (al-ya's) from the spirit of Allah, while they deny the name of disbelief (kufr) [for the sinner] – and Allah Almighty said: 'And none despairs of the mercy of Allah except the disbelieving people' – is a contradictory saying, for Allah has combined disbelief and despair; so whoever affirms one of them is necessarily bound by the other. Since it is established with us and with them that he is not a disbeliever – for disbelief in common usage is denial (takdhib), and the committer of a major sin is in a state of affirmation (tasdiq) while hoping for His forgiveness and fearing His punishment, and knows that whoever despairs of his Lord's mercy is misguided and ignorant of Allah – it is established that he is not a denier. And in reality, disbelief is a name for covering (al-satr), and the committer of a major sin does not cover any of his Lord's blessings nor deny His right. So it is invalid that he should be a disbeliever. Likewise, faith in common usage and in the revealed law (al-sam') is affirmation (tasdiq), and it is known that he has not denied Allah in anything; it is established that he is a believer. And Allah is the Grantor of success. The truth is to say: All the Khawarij and Mu'tazila, when they commit major sins, are disbelievers according to their own claim, deserving of eternity in the Fire. And others from among the various sects who claim Islam are not [like that]. For reasons, one of which is that they unanimously agree upon denying mercy from Allah, and that is the description of disbelief as mentioned in the verse, and by His saying: 'And those who disbelieve in the signs of Allah and meeting Him – those have despaired of My mercy.' So the name [of disbelief] applies to both parties.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage presents several consecutive arguments. First, al-Maturidi presents a second type of proof: Allah has obligated many acts of worship under the name of faith (al-iman), and the knowledge of what is lawful and unlawful is often tied to the presence or absence of faith. Yet those who commit acts of sin (fisq) are still included in these obligations together with the believers. This shows that the name of faith is not removed from them. Second, he invokes the consensus (ijma') of the community: the practice of praying over deceased Muslims, seeking forgiveness for them, and affirming intercession (al-shafa'ah) proves that they are considered believers, for the community does not pray over disbelievers. Third, he refutes the Mu'tazila: they claim that major sinners are not disbelievers (kuffar) and yet they also say that such sinners are in a state of despair (ya's) from Allah's mercy. But Allah has connected despair with disbelief in the Quran (Surah Yusuf 12:87): 'and none despairs of the mercy of Allah except the disbelieving people.' Therefore, if they affirm despair, they must also affirm disbelief, which they deny – a contradiction. Al-Maturidi explains that in common usage (al-'urf), disbelief is denial (takdhib), but the major sinner affirms (musaddiq) the truth and hopes for mercy, so he is not a denier. Furthermore, the linguistic root of kufr means 'covering' (al-satr), and the sinner does not cover Allah's blessings or deny His rights. Hence he cannot be a kafir. Likewise, faith linguistically and in the revealed law means affirmation (tasdiq), and the sinner has not denied anything, so he remains a believer. Finally, al-Maturidi makes a striking conclusion: according to the logic of the Khawarij and Mu'tazila themselves, when they commit major sins, they become disbelievers (since they hold that major sins expel from faith), and they are deserving of eternal punishment. The Ahl al-Sunnah, however, are not like that, because they do not despair of Allah's mercy, which would be the characteristic of disbelief as per the Quran.

Key Terms
الإيمان
الفسق
العبادات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that committing a major sin removes one from the category of faith entirely.
Correction: Al-Maturidi shows that since sinners are still obligated to perform acts of worship under the name of faith, they remain within the fold of faith.

Checkpoint
According to al-Maturidi's second proof, what indicates that the name of faith is not removed from major sinners?
A) They still pray and are addressed by the same obligations.
B) They never commit sins.
C) They are called believers by the Prophet.
D) They are punished in this world.

Key Takeaway
The continuation of religious obligations upon sinners demonstrates that they still bear the name of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you have sinned, have you ever felt that your faith is completely gone or that your prayers are meaningless? How does this passage challenge that feeling? What concrete step will you take to remind yourself that your faith remains and your worship is still valid?
?
This proof shows that the same obligations apply to sinners and righteous believers. Do you treat others who sin with the same expectation of worship, or do you consider them as no longer part of the faith? How can you change your view to align with this teaching?
?
If you knew that a fellow Muslim committed a major sin, would you still encourage them to pray and fast? Why or why not? What does this passage say about your responsibility towards them?

The Consensus of the Community: Intercession and Prayer for Deceased Muslims
Al-Maturidi presents the consensus of the community as evidence for the faith of major sinners.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the consensus of the Muslim community in praying for deceased Muslims and affirming intercession proves that major sinners are believers.

Core Idea
The community's practice shows that sinners are treated as believers even after death.

Imam al-Maturidi now invokes the consensus (ijma') of the Muslim community. The consistent practice of the ummah—praying over all who die facing the qibla, seeking forgiveness for them, and affirming intercession—proves that they are considered believers. This consensus is powerful evidence for those who do not reject authentic reports and the guidance of the imams. Let's explore this argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the consensus practice
Read the passage and note what practices al-Maturidi mentions as evidence of consensus.
The practices include praying over the deceased, seeking forgiveness, and affirming intercession.
2
Understand the implication
Reflect on the fact that the community does not pray over disbelievers. Therefore, praying over all who die from the people of the qibla indicates they are believers.
3
Consider the authority of consensus
Al-Maturidi presents this as a strong proof for those who accept authentic hadith and the guidance of imams.

Refuting the Mu'tazila: Despair and Disbelief Are Inseparable
Al-Maturidi refutes the Mu'tazila on the relationship between despair and disbelief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Maturidi refutes the Mu'tazila by showing that claiming sinners despair of mercy implies they are disbelievers, which contradicts their own position.

Core Idea
The Quran links despair with disbelief; thus Mu'tazila contradict themselves.

Imam al-Maturidi now directly refutes the Mu'tazila. They claim that major sinners are not disbelievers yet also assert that such sinners are in a state of despair (ya's) from Allah's mercy. Al-Maturidi points out that the Quran explicitly states that only disbelievers despair of Allah's mercy (Surah Yusuf 12:87). Therefore, if the Mu'tazila affirm despair, they must also affirm disbelief, leading to a contradiction. Let's examine this argument and the linguistic definitions that follow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Mu'tazila claim
Read the passage and note what the Mu'tazila say about major sinners regarding despair and disbelief.
They say sinners despair of mercy but are not disbelievers.
2
Observe the Quranic verse
Al-Maturidi cites Quran 12:87 which directly links despair with disbelief.
3
Understand the contradiction
If despair is affirmed, disbelief must be affirmed, but the Mu'tazila deny disbelief. This shows their position is logically inconsistent.
4
Learn the linguistic definitions
Al-Maturidi explains that kufr means denial (takdhib) and covering (satr), and the sinner does neither, so he cannot be a kafir. Faith means affirmation (tasdiq), so the sinner remains a believer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Then the consensus of the transmitters in affirming intercession (al-shafa'ah), and the continuous practice of the community in praying over all who die from the people of the qibla, and seeking forgiveness for them, and asking mercy for them – this is the evidence for one whose soul refuses to deny the authentic reports and to oppose the guiding imams. And there is no power except with Allah. Then the saying of the Mu'tazila about the realization of despair (al-ya's) from the spirit of Allah, while they deny the name of disbelief (kufr) [for the sinner] – and Allah Almighty said: 'And none despairs of the mercy of Allah except the disbelieving people' – is a contradictory saying, for Allah has combined disbelief and despair; so whoever affirms one of them is necessarily bound by the other. Since it is established with us and with them that he is not a disbeliever – for disbelief in common usage is denial (takdhib), and the committer of a major sin is in a state of affirmation (tasdiq) while hoping for His forgiveness and fearing His punishment, and knows that whoever despairs of his Lord's mercy is misguided and ignorant of Allah – it is established that he is not a denier. And in reality, disbelief is a name for covering (al-satr), and the committer of a major sin does not cover any of his Lord's blessings nor deny His right. So it is invalid that he should be a disbeliever. Likewise, faith in common usage and in the revealed law (al-sam') is affirmation (tasdiq), and it is known that he has not denied Allah in anything; it is established that he is a believer. And Allah is the Grantor of success. The truth is to say: All the Khawarij and Mu'tazila, when they commit major sins, are disbelievers according to their own claim, deserving of eternity in the Fire. And others from among the various sects who claim Islam are not [like that]. For reasons, one of which is that they unanimously agree upon denying mercy from Allah, and that is the description of disbelief as mentioned in the verse, and by His saying: 'And those who disbelieve in the signs of Allah and meeting Him – those have despaired of My mercy.' So the name [of disbelief] applies to both parties.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage presents several consecutive arguments. First, al-Maturidi presents a second type of proof: Allah has obligated many acts of worship under the name of faith (al-iman), and the knowledge of what is lawful and unlawful is often tied to the presence or absence of faith. Yet those who commit acts of sin (fisq) are still included in these obligations together with the believers. This shows that the name of faith is not removed from them. Second, he invokes the consensus (ijma') of the community: the practice of praying over deceased Muslims, seeking forgiveness for them, and affirming intercession (al-shafa'ah) proves that they are considered believers, for the community does not pray over disbelievers. Third, he refutes the Mu'tazila: they claim that major sinners are not disbelievers (kuffar) and yet they also say that such sinners are in a state of despair (ya's) from Allah's mercy. But Allah has connected despair with disbelief in the Quran (Surah Yusuf 12:87): 'and none despairs of the mercy of Allah except the disbelieving people.' Therefore, if they affirm despair, they must also affirm disbelief, which they deny – a contradiction. Al-Maturidi explains that in common usage (al-'urf), disbelief is denial (takdhib), but the major sinner affirms (musaddiq) the truth and hopes for mercy, so he is not a denier. Furthermore, the linguistic root of kufr means 'covering' (al-satr), and the sinner does not cover Allah's blessings or deny His rights. Hence he cannot be a kafir. Likewise, faith linguistically and in the revealed law means affirmation (tasdiq), and the sinner has not denied anything, so he remains a believer. Finally, al-Maturidi makes a striking conclusion: according to the logic of the Khawarij and Mu'tazila themselves, when they commit major sins, they become disbelievers (since they hold that major sins expel from faith), and they are deserving of eternal punishment. The Ahl al-Sunnah, however, are not like that, because they do not despair of Allah's mercy, which would be the characteristic of disbelief as per the Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila believe they can hold that sinners despair of mercy without calling them disbelievers.
Correction: Al-Maturidi shows this is impossible because the Quran explicitly ties despair to disbelief.

Checkpoint
What verse does al-Maturidi use to show the connection between despair and disbelief?
A) Quran 39:53
B) Quran 12:87
C) Quran 2:286
D) Quran 4:48

Key Takeaway
Despair of Allah's mercy is inherently linked to disbelief; therefore, the Mu'tazila cannot separate the two.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt a moment of despair, thinking that Allah will not forgive you? How does this lesson's teaching that despair is linked to disbelief shake you out of that state? What will you do the next time that feeling creeps in?
?
The lesson says that a major sinner, because he affirms the truth, is still a believer. But what about your own heart: do you truly affirm and hope, or have you let despair settle in while still mouthing words of faith? Can you honestly say you fear punishment and hope for mercy as the passage describes?
?
If disbelief is 'covering' Allah's blessings, in what ways might you be 'covering' – ignoring or downplaying – the mercy and favors Allah has shown you today? What would it look like to uncover them and respond with gratitude and hope?
